All Reviews

  1. I was given a gel kit for Christmas last year and went online to purchase a light. There were so many options and prices ranging from $20-250+ for UV and LED lights. After reading reviews and researching the options I decided to get this particular light. After using it for about 4 months here's what I think of it:<br /><br />Positives:<br /> -Convenience: I was hooked on being to cure both my hands at once. I am already annoyed that I have to take off my old polish one hand at a time, I don't think I could handle having to cure and hand at a time also (except maybe with a quick curing LED).<br /> -Wattage: I've seen UV lamps with wattage as low as 9 and as high as about 54. This lamp is 45 watts, which seems powerful enough to accomplish what I want.<br /> -Settings: I use the 2 minute setting for everything and I've never had any problems. There's also a 3 minute and continuous setting. I'm glad I don't have to look at the clock or set a stopwatch to time myself.<br /> -Price: After spending a few hours researching these lamps I realized this is probably has the best features for the price. There are models from $20 up to about $300 (LED usually), this seemed to have everything I need for about $50. That's just a little over the price of one gel manicure at the salon.<br /> -Works with all my polish: I mostly have Gelish prodcuts, but also bought Red Carpet and FingerPaints products, which cure equally as well under this light.<br /><br />Cons:<br /> -UV vs LED: In hindsight I wish I would've sprung for a LED light. The bulbs last much longer, there's no cancer causing UV rays and the drying time is much quicker. The better LED lights are $60+, but I did see one that got pretty good reviews for about $33. The lower priced LED lamps generally only do one hand at a time, up to 4 fingers at a time (thumb separate). I'm not entirely sure if I'd be happy having to put my hand under a lamp 4 times for each coat of polish I do, even if it's for less time. The LED I want is $270 and does one whole hand at a time, 30 seconds each coat. Now that I've grown to love and rely on my gel manicures I know it's probably going to eventually be worth the extra investment.<br /> -Bulbs: I can't say exactly how long these bulbs will last, but the replacements are sure pricey. I looked it up and each bulb is right now $11.21, so the cost of 3 new bulbs will be $33.63. This is just a quick Amazon search, I didn't do any major price comparisons. That's not much cheaper than the cost of the whole unit plus bulbs. I think when I get to the point of needing to replace them I will be giving my unit away and upgrading to my desired LED dyer.<br /> -Size: Both a positive and negative, yes, you can dry both hands at once, but this thing is pretty big to store. If you are short on space this might not be the best option out there.<br /><br />All things considered, I'm not unhappy with my purchase and am giving 4 stars for &#34;I like it&#34;. I wasn't sure if I was going to like doing my own manicures or if I would do it a couple times and would get bored of it, so I didn't want to spend too much on a light. Now that I know I'm going to be doing my own gel manicures for years to come, I will eventually upgrade. For anyone who wants a relatively inexpensive, larger, 2 handed UV lamp, I definitely recommend this unit. If you have the cash to spend it might be better just to initially go with the LED.<br /><br />Update: I did end up getting the Gelish light for about $200. I wish I would've got it so much sooner! This UV light did serve me well, but when I got my LED I was in heaven. Now repairing a nail is a breeze and do nail art since it cures so quickly. The times for that are: base coat 5 seconds, color 20-30 seconds, top coat 30 seconds. I also like doing one hand at a time so much more. I can scrape the extra paint off with my opposite hand. If you think you're going to be doing gel for a long time I recommend splurging for the better light. Igave this away and it's still going strong though.

  37. After reading the reviews, I purchased this dryer. And so far, so good. It was easy to get the bulbs in, and it seems to work well and quickly. Another reviewer, Arbonne Girl, provides great step-by-step instructions for getting the polish on. I followed her suggestions exactly and ended up with a terrific looking manicure. I thought I'd provide some suggestions for removal, as I saw some reviewers said they were having trouble getting the polish off. So try this: 1. Use a nail buffing block (medium/medium fine grit) and buff the shine off of your nails. 2. Cut 10 small pieces of cotton and 10 squares of tin foil. Saturate the cotton with acetone and place a piece on each nail, then wrap with the tin foil. Let the cotton/foil sit on your nails for a couple of minutes. 3. Remove one cotton/foil at a time and lightly scrape the polish from the nail. This is going to seem random, but I happened to have a metal dog dental tooth scaler (also purchased from Amazon), and it worked perfectly to scrape the loose polish off my nails. Now I just have to get a new scaler for my dog's teeth :). 4. Use one of the pieces of cotton to clean off any bits of remaining polish.

During my research, I visited the CND Shellac website, where they recommend their own U/V nail dryer for use with their shellac. After more research, I decided to save myself a considerable amount of money and purchased the Thermal Spa 49135 U/V Gel Light Nail Dryer from Amazon. At this point I need to qualify this review with the following: I am, by no means, a professional nail technician. The initial investment was pricey (I paid roughly 125.00 for the nail dryer and the CND base coat, CND top coat and CND Shellac), but I figure I'll make most of my money back after the second use. Not a bad ROI. Next, the manicure process may be a bit more time-consuming than a regular manicure, due to the curing time required for the product, but really is no more difficult to perform than painting one's nails with regular polish. It is IMPERATIVE that you follow the directions when using the shellac products, but, if you do, you can end up with results that look fabulous for a fraction of the cost of a spa visit. Bottom line, save yourself some money - this Thermal Spa 49135 Professional U/V Gel Light Nail Dryer works wonderfully with the CND Shellac products.

  233. After much research, I decided to buy this UV lamp system. I did not want a lamp shipped from Hong Kong. and I wanted a brand name. Always mix the bottles, I have had the nails flake off after about a week because the polish was not well mixed. 2. I use the Harmony / Gelish pH balance before I put the base coat on. This basically takes any moisture or oils out of your nail and makes them an acidic pH. Its cheap too 3. Gelish Basecoat , a very thin layer and dry for 1 to 2 min. This lamp does not have a one minute timer .... I wish it did 4. Polish Coat.... again a very thin layer and BE SURE to try and wrap the polish around to the top edge of your nail. This creates a seal and will cause less chipping. Be sure to dry for the full two mintues for each coat. Do a three minute dry if you are using a dark polish 5. Gelish Top Coat.... this bring you the shine you want. Super thin layers are key and wrap that top coat over the edge/ tip of your nail. Hope this helps

  279. I'm not a professional nail artist, however enjoy getting pedicures in the summer months. I just dont Like the price tag that comes with a pedicure, that only last 7-10 days. I've watched nail professionals use a machine similar to this one. So, I researched and watch several Gel Nail Polish videos and techniques, and said this can't be too hard to do at home. I ordered this UV lamp, 1 bottle of Harmony Gelish nail polish color and 1 bottle of CND Shellac Gel nail Polish color, Harmony foundation and Harmony top coat. The price of Harmony and Shellac polish are about $12-15/bottle of nail color. You get your money's worth with Harmony Gelish nail polish, because their bottles are twice as big (15 ml, compared to the 7.5 ml bottle Shellac has). The polishes wear the same and have the same quality, and last just as long.<br /><br />This UV lamp works wonderfully. I've been impressed with this lamp. So this summer, I will not be going to the nail salon for pedicures. Both Harmony and Shellac gel polish are nice and easy to apply. I've done 2 pedicures on myself so far and have turned out beautifully (actually better than the professional pedicures).<br /><br />Steps for Gel Nails<br />1. Clean nail with alcohol, nail polish remover, or apply dehydrating coat.<br />2. Apply foundation / base coat to nail. Cure for 2 minutes.<br />3. Apply thin layer of color polish. Cure for 2 minutes. (nail will feel sticky/tacky, this is normal)<br />4. Apply 2nd coat of color polish. Cure for 2 minutes. (repeat if you desire).<br />5. Apply clear top coat. Cure for 2-3 minutes. (nails will feel sticky/tacky still, this is normal)<br />6. Remove sticky/tacky coat by using rubbing alcohol 70% or stronger. Saturate a small piece of clean paper towel with alcohol, and wipe each nail. This will remove the sticky/tacky substance, and you will have a shiny beautiful nail.<br /><br />Removal of Gel Nail Polish<br />1. Saturate a cotton ball or cotton swab with 100% acetone.<br />2. Apply toeach nail, wrap foil around it to secure in place and leave on for 10-15 minutes.<br />3. Rub at cotton ball/cotton swab as you remove it and gel polish comes off nicely. If you have a little color remaining, just get a wooden cuticle stick and rub at it and it will come right off.<br />** I rather use Handsdown Soak Off Nail Wraps instead of cotton ball and foil in removing gel polish. They are much easier to use and without the mess you get when using cotton balls and foil. However, cost concerning they are expensive $25/box of 100.

  431. After reading the reviews, I purchased this UV dryer. I just wanted to leave a little more feedback on this dryer in regards to shellac nail polish. I bought this product to do my own nails. I am not a nail tech, but fully capable of doing my own nails. So here is what I did, I purchased the shellac scrub fresh nail prep, shellac UV base coat, shellac red barroness nail color, shellac UV top coat and this dryer all from Amazon sellers. Here is what I did step by step and it worked.<br />1. Follow Shellac's instruction on how to prep nails and use products-go to their website. I shape my nails and cuticles, then use scrub fresh to clean and dehydrate.<br />2. SHAKE the UV base coat for two minutes and paint both hands! I didn't shake well the the first time and the base coat and nail color came out too thick.<br />3. I put nails under light to cure for 30 seconds. Nails will feel tacky (not dry) and this is normal. Has to do with oxygenation with curing.<br />4. Shake color -paint one coat of color on both hands and put under light for two minutes-nails will feel tacky. This is normal.<br />5. Shake color-paint second coat of color on both hands and put under light for two minutes-nails will feel tacky. This is normal.<br />6. Shake top coat-paint top coat on nails-place under dryer for two minutes. Use 99% alcohol to remove tacky layer on top coat. I used 70% alcohol pads and this worked fine! A tiny bit of nail color streak came off on alcohol pad but I continued on removing tacky layer. When I was finished, nails were perfectly cured. Polish has been on for 10 days and still look brand new. If nails lose their shine due to lotion...-wife off with alcohol pad and they look brand new.<br />7. When ready to take off-either soak off with 100%acetone on cotton balls with aluminum foil or soak fingers in acetone. I wouldn't bother with the CND pad removers.<br />Bottom line-this lamp works great for Shellac nails-no need to buy $200 plus one. You will read so many mixed reviews about why you shouldn't be doing it yourself and using anything but the CND dryer, but this is what worked for me.<br />Good Luckso many mixed reviews about why you shouldn't be doing it yourself and using anything but the CND dryer, but this is what worked for me.<br />Good Luck

  485. I received this curing light in the mail today and figured I'd give it a whirl. I used the CND Shellac system to do an American manicure. I had seen the manicure done several times but had never attempted it. Shellac is relatively forgiving as long as you apply it thin. I'm not stating this is the right or wrong way, but this is how I've seen it done most often. I did one hand start to finish and then the other for sake of ease and to prevent flaws. 1. Trimmed back cuticles, shaped the nails, and lightly buffed with a black buffing block just to remove shine. 2. Wash hands with soap and water, dry thoroughly. Wipe each nail with a bit of paper towel soaked in 90% isopropyl alcohol (I cut a sheet of paper towel into a bunch of little squares.) 3. Shake shake shake that base coat bottle 'til your arm hurts. 4. Apply a thin coat of base coat to the nails on one hand. Cure for 30 seconds. 5. After shaking and shaking, and shaking...apply Cream Puff thinly (just thick enough that it is opaque; this will probably take a little practice) to the nail tips (you can look on YouTube to get an idea of how to angle the brush). 6. Use a manicure brush dipped in 90% isopropyl alcohol and then blotted on paper towel to refine the line, coming from the knuckle side and making small circular touches to smooth the line into a nice curve. 7. Cure for 2 minutes. You can do minor touch ups with the Cream Puff and re-cure for 2 minutes. 8. Shake up the top coat. You can apply this just a tiny bit thicker than the other coats, but make sure to smooth it out nicely. 9. Cure for 6 minutes. Yes, 6 minutes. 10. Soak another bit of paper towel with 90% IPA, wipe down those nails until you remove the tacky layer. 11. Repeat on the other hand. 12. If you like, apply cuticle oil and lotion. It's good to moisturize your nails after they've been exposed to so much alcohol. 13. Marvel in the fact that you accomplished something you normally pay $40-60 for someone else to do. Like I said, I'm not a nail technician and I didn't go to cosmetology school. But I am pretty satisfied with the outcome. This is a fantastic product so enjoy it. Be patient and remember that practice makes perfect!

  547. I read a few other reviews where the bulbs would flicker or not turn on. Other users said they had to jiggle them a bit to get them to start. This is true, as I am having the same problem. I get the same results as the lights in the salon. I think the price can't be beat. My mom can buy at the beauty supply wholesale stores and their lamps are all $200 - $400. This one does the same thing for a fraction of the cost. I have been using the Gelish System with this lamp and it's been fine. I did just use a CND Shellac color this last time. I don't know if it's because it's a better product, or I'm just getting better at application, but this manicure seems to be the best. I am going to try another CND Shellac color. I've have learned the hard way -- there are few tips I wish someone would have shared with me.<br /><br />1. When removing nail polish, soak part of a cotton ball in acetone. Place directly on nail and wrap with foil. Sit for about 10 minutes. It makes removal SO much easier. And it's better for your hands because not so much is exposed to pure acetone.<br /><br />2. When you start put all the cotton balls away. Don't have any cotton balls near year. The first few times, bits of cotton got into the color and top coats and then the manicure looks like a total \\"at home\\" job. Trust me, it will find it's way. I clean my nails with a nail brush just prior to starting.<br /><br />3. Don't waste your money on the prep wipes. It's just alcohol. After filing, shaping and cuticle trimming. Wash hands. Dry with towel and apply a swipe of acetone or alcohol to nail bed. Let dry and begin.<br /><br />4. Use VERY THIN coats on all steps. Once it gets \\"gloopy\\" you might as well start over.<br /><br />5. The process is no where near as \\"forgiving\\" as traditional nail polish. Once it's cured - it's cured. So, if you go off your nail a bit, fix it before it goes under the light. If part of it goes over to your skin it won't seal properly and it will just pop off in a day or two. Esp true with the top coat. A little goes a long way and good luck keeping it \\"in the lines.\\"<br /><br />6. You have to get good cuticle nippers and a good cuticle remover gel. Take your time on this step (remember, not as forgiving as traditional nail polish). If you have cuticles, you will get paint on them - it won't seal and in two days you won't be happy.<br /><br />7. You can use the 70% rubbing alcohol to cure it, however, if you can find 91% or higher it's worth the extra $1.00. I found some at wal-mart. Soak the cotton and don't be afraid to rub the nail. It won't ruin it and it will cure it better.<br /><br />Hope this helps!<br /><br />UPDATE: Don't buy this lamp! It has been a little over a month and about 6 uses...when I turned it on tonight, it flickered and wouldn't turn on. Completely dead. I was worried because it was outside the 30 day window. I called Amazon and becuase it was fullfilled by them they are standing by their products and refunding me my money. THANK YOU AMAZON FOR BEING A COMPANY THAT I CAN TRUST AND WHICH VALUES THEIR CUSTOMERS. Whew! I could have been out $60.00!

Someone said it was hard to take off but what you need to do to remove shellac polish cnd/ and or OPI polish first you need to rub your nails with acetone, then place cotton balls full of acetone on each finger wrap them with alumininum foil. Let them soak for at least 15-20 min. (Some peoples nail time vary). Then you take a metal cuticle pusher(after you have removed cotton and aluminum foils) you will notice that polish has become much softer so then you lightly push off polish and you'll see that your nails are not damaged! Unlike acrylic, shellac is much more convenient for your nails. By the way I am a licensed cosmetologist I hope the info on taking off polish has helped!

  833. As a gel nail polish newbie, I read all the reviews and ultimately purchased the Thermal Spa 49135 U/V Gel Light Nail Dryer, then purchased Shellac polish from the CND line to use with it. Others have described the process, so I won't go into that. Finding the bulbs under the false floor of the box and inserting them in the machine was a no brainer. I'm not sure what all the fuss was about in some other reviews. Really, folks, come on. How hard can it be?<br />It was difficult to believe that the process would yield results including two full weeks of perfect nails, but it's really true! When selecting which gel light machine to purchase, I was not at all sure whether I would prefer a machine that could handle only one hand, or one that could manage two, especially since the larger machine is pretty big, and I would have to find a place to store it (Think smallish toaster oven). When I started using my new machine, it all came clear. If you're trying to decide on this point, here's what I recommend: if you're doing your own nails, you might want to consider using a machine that can handle both hands. If someone else is working on your nails, a one-hander would be work just fine, but I still recommend this machine for its value.<br />A few other tips: The instructions on how to apply polish say to wipe the nails with alcohol as the final step, to eliminate the tackiness. \\"Really?\\", I said? It seemed so counter-intuitive. Well, it's true folks. You really put a cotton pad saturated with alcohol right on that sticky, tacky nail that you've just finished, and wipe off the tackiness. I even had to go look at a YouTube video of the process to be certain that this was what they wanted you to do. It is! Also, don't forget to put polish on the front edges of your nails, for a better seal. Otherwise, the layers have an occasional tendency to lift.<br />All in all, a great machine, good quality construction, a great buy, and I am now a gel nail convert. My nails are looking better than they have in a long time, and I can just get on with my life, doing the things I normally do.
